      if(window.addEventListener) {

              <a class="pin-it-button" count-layout="horizontal" href="http://pinterest.com/pin/create/button/?url=http://www.closetcooking.com/2009/09/kolokythokeftedes-zucchini-and-feta.html&amp;description=Kolokythokeftedes (Zucchini and Feta Balls)" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">
              </a>
             </div>
             <div class="sm_gp1">
              <a class="g-plusone" data-href="http://www.closetcooking.com/2009/09/kolokythokeftedes-zucchini-and-feta.html" data-size="medium" href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://www.closetcooking.com/2009/09/kolokythokeftedes-zucchini-and-feta.html" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">
              </a>
             </div>
            </div>
            <div style="clear: both;">
            </div>
           </div>
           <p>
           </p>
           <div class="recipe_post">
            <div class="story">
             <img alt="Kolokythokeftedes (Zucchini and Feta Balls)" class="photo" height="333" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_UIXOn06Pz70/SrLWQBKPgGI/AAAAAAAAIlA/63InrUWbY88/s800/Kolokythokeftedes+(Zucchini+and+Feta+Balls)+1+500.jpg" title="Kolokythokeftedes (Zucchini and Feta Balls)" width="500"/>
             <br/>
             <br/>
             <div style="width:100%;text-align: center;">
              <a href="http://pinterest.com/ClosetCooking/">
               <img alt="Follow Me on Pinterest" height="26" src="http://passets-cdn.pinterest.com/images/follow-on-pinterest-button.png" style="border:none;" width="156"/>
              </a>
             </div>
             <br/>
             When I went to Greece on vacation last year, at one of the restaurants we went to we decided to skip having a main course and we ordered a bunch of mezes or appetizers to share. Among the appetizers were of course some of the classics including
             <a href="http://www.closetcooking.com/2007/05/tzatziki-sauce.html">
              tzatziki
             </a>
             (a Greek cucumber salad),
             <a href="http://www.closetcooking.com/2007/08/melitzanosalata.html">
              melitzanosalata
             </a>
             (a Greek roasted eggplant salad) and a few others. The one that really caught my attention however was the zucchini balls otherwise know as kolokythokeftedes. They were like meatballs only made with zucchini along with some herbs and feta. They were perfectly round, golden brown, slightly crispy on the outside and warm, soft, moist and tasty on the inside. The zucchini balls were so good and luckily I got to have a lot of them as many at the table passed on them when they heard that they were made with zucchini.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             <a name="more">
             </a>
             I had been meaning to try making the kolokithokeftedes at home for a while and now that zucchini season is running out it was time to get to making them. I pretty much just started with the recipe that I used for my
             <a href="http://www.closetcooking.com/2008/08/greek-zucchini-fritters-with-tzatziki.html">
              Greek style zucchini fritters
             </a>
             and modified it slightly for the zucchini balls. Where the zucchini fritters could be fairly liquidy and even be poured into the pan to fry the zucchini balls needed to be able to hold their form so I kept adding equal parts whole wheat flour and whole wheat bread crumbs until the mixture could hold the form of a ball. I also added a splash of ouzo to the batter to add a hint of anise that would add that something special that you just can't quite put your finger on. Despite the fact that my skills at forming perfect balls falls a bit short, the zucchini balls tasted great! I served them with some tzatziki to dip them in and they made a really nice snack. They would also make for a nice light meal. It is always fun trying to recreate dishes that you remember fondly from another time!
             <br/>
             <br/>
            </div>
            <div class="recipe" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/Recipe">
             <img alt="Kolokythokeftedes (Zucchini and Feta Balls)" class="photo recipe_photo" itemprop="image" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_UIXOn06Pz70/SrLWQBKPgGI/AAAAAAAAIlA/63InrUWbY88/s800/Kolokythokeftedes+(Zucchini+and+Feta+Balls)+1+500.jpg" title="Kolokythokeftedes (Zucchini and Feta Balls)" width="250"/>
             <h4 class="fn name recipe_title" itemprop="name">
              Kolokythokeftedes (Zucchini and Feta Balls)
             </h4>
             <div class="details">
              <span class="time">
               <b>
                Prep Time
               </b>
               :
               <meta content="PT10M" itemprop="prepTime"/>
               10 minutes
              </span>
              <span class="time">
               <b>
                Cook Time
               </b>
               :
               <meta content="PT15M" itemprop="cookTime"/>
               15 minutes
              </span>
              <span class="time">
               <b>
                Total Time
               </b>
               :
               <meta content="PT25M" itemprop="totalTime"/>
               25 minutes
              </span>
              <span class="yield">
               <b>
                Servings
               </b>
               :
               <span itemprop="recipeYield">
                4
               </span>
              </span>
             </div>
             <p class="summary" itemprop="description">
              Zucchini, feta and plenty of fresh herbs rolled into balls and fried until light and crispy and golden brown! These zucchini balls are a great appetizer and can be served with tzatziki or marina sauce for dipping.
             </p>
             <div class="buttonbar">
              <a class="print_recipe_button" href="javascript:void(0);">
               <img src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-jUDlms8VMSE/UjLhhSlEBxI/AAAAAAAAaPc/Rs70snnZGLo/s160/print_recipe-small.png"/>
              </a>
             </div>
             <h5>
              ingredients
             </h5>
             <ul class="ingredients">
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               2 cups zucchini, grated and squeezed
              </li>
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               1/4 cup of feta, crumbled
              </li>
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               1 splash ouzo (optional)
              </li>
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               1 clove garlic, chopped
              </li>
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               2 green onions, sliced
              </li>
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               1 handful herbs (such as mint, dill and parsley), chopped
              </li>
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               1 egg, lightly beaten
              </li>
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               salt and pepper to taste
              </li>
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               ~1/2 cup flour (I used whole wheat)
              </li>
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               breadcrumbs (I use whole wheat)
              </li>
              <li itemprop="ingredients">
               oil for frying
              </li>
             </ul>
             <h5>
              directions
             </h5>
             <ol class="instructions">
              <li itemprop="recipeInstructions">
               Mix the zucchini, feta, ouzo, garlic, green onion, herbs and egg and season with salt and pepper.
              </li>
              <li itemprop="recipeInstructions">
               Mix in enough flour and breadcrumbs that you can work with the mixture to form balls.
              </li>
              <li itemprop="recipeInstructions">
               Form the mixture into balls and dust in flour.
              </li>
              <li itemprop="recipeInstructions">
               Fry in oil until golden brown and set aside to cool.
              </li>
             </ol>
            </div>

           </dt>
           <dd class="comment-body">
            <p>
             hello, Kevin! i love your blog and i really really like the fact that, being Greek, while i browsed through your greek/greek-inspired recipes, i discovered that you do a really good job interpreting the ingredients and cooking style! i know i'm being picky many times when i look at foreign blogs and see that their "greek" recipes seem very far from the original, but that certainly isn't the case here, so thank you very much :)
             <br/>
             all the ranting aside, i just wanted to clarify the kolokythokeftedes pronunciation problem!
             <br/>
             You see, this is a composite word, consisting of the words "kolokythi" ( = zucchini) and "keftedes" ( = food balls), so the right pronunciation would be ko-lo-ki-tho-ke-ftE-des, with the "th" in "tho" being from the letter "" so it gets pronounced like in "thatch" and not in "the"! i really do hope i clarified this :)
            </p>
           </dd>

        <h2>
         About Me
        </h2>
        <div class="widget-content">
         <a href="https://plus.google.com/106383062414578378285">
          <img alt="My Photo" class="profile-img" height="80" src="//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-Wu3FhyMVY20/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAUoA/mlkFa1gsE94/s80-c/photo.jpg" width="80"/>
         </a>
         <dl class="profile-datablock">
          <dt class="profile-data">
           <a class="profile-name-link" href="https://plus.google.com/106383062414578378285/?rel=author" rel="author">
            Kevin Lynch+
           </a>
          </dt>
          <dd class="profile-textblock">
           <span>
            I came to realize that my meals were boring and that I had been eating the same few dishes over and over again for years. It was time for a change! I now spend my free time searching for, creating and trying tasty new recipes in my closet sized kitchen.
           </span>
          </dd>
